\\treturn framework.Queue, nil\\n370: }\\n371: \\n372: func buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\\n373: \\tqueueingHintMap := \\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\\n442: \\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\\n443: \\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\\n444: \\t// framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable).WithError(err)\\n173: \\t\\t}\\n174: \\n175: \\t\\t// Run PostFilter plugins to attempt to make the pod schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\\n176: \\t\\tresult, status := fwk.RunPostFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod, fitError.Diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\\n177: \\t\\tmsg := status.Message()\\n178: \\t\\tfitError.Diagnosis.PostFilterMsg = msg\\n179: nominatingInfo}, podInfo, framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable).WithError(err)\\n190: \\t}\\n191: \\n192: \\tmetrics.SchedulingAlgorithmLatency.Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\\n193: \\t// Tell the cache to assume that a pod now is running on a given node, even though it hasn't been bound yet.\\n194: \\t// This allows us to keep scheduling without waiting on binding to occur.\\n195: \\tassumedPodInfo := podInfo.DeepCopy()\\n196: \\tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\\n197: \\t// assume modifies `assumedPod` by setting NodeName=scheduleResult.SuggestedHost\\n198: \\terr = sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\\n199: \\tif err != nil {\\n200: \\t\\t// This is most probably result of a BUG in retrying logic.\\n201: \\t\\t// We report an assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\\n212: \\t\\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\\n213: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \\\"Scheduler cache \\t\\t\\t}\\n224: \\t\\t\\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(sts)\\n225: \\t\\t\\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(sts.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\\n226: \\t\\t}\\n227: \\t\\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, sts\\n228: \\t}\\n229: \\n230: \\t// Run \\\"permit\\\" plugins.\\n231: \\trunPermitStatus := fwk.RunPermitPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\\n232: \\tif !runPermitStatus.IsWait() && !runPermitStatus.IsSuccess() \\t}\\n253: \\n254: \\t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\\n255: \\tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\\n256: \\t\\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, nil\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\\n266: \\tctx context.Context,\\n267: \\tstate *framework.CycleState,\\n268: \\tfwk framework.Framework,\\n269: \\tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\\n270: \\tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\\n271: \\tstart time.Time,\\n272: \\tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) \\t\\t\\t})\\n350: \\t\\t} else {\\n351: \\t\\t\\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\\n352: \\t\\t}\\n353: \\t}\\n354: \\n355: \\tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\\n356: }\\n357: \\n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\\n359: Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all extenders scores for all nodes.\n791: \t\t// It is keyed with node name.\n792: \t\tallNodeExtendersScores := make(map[string]*framework.NodePluginScores, len(nodes))\n793: \t\tvar mu sync.Mutex\n794: \t\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n795: \t\tfor i := range extenders {\n796: \t\t\tif !extenders[i].IsInterested(pod) {\n797: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n798: \t\t\t}\n799: \t\t\twg.Add(1)\n800: \t\t\tgo func(extIndex int) {\n801: \t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Inc()\n802: \t\t\t\tdefer func() {\n803: \t\t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Dec()\n804: \t\t\t\t\twg.Done()\n805: \t\t\t\t}()\n806: \t\t\t\tprioritizedList, weight, err := extenders[extIndex].Prioritize(pod, nodes)\n807: \t\t\t\tif err != nil {\n808: \t\t\t\t\t// Prioritization errors from extender can be ignored, let k8s/other extenders determine the priorities\n809: \t\t\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Failed to run extender's priority function. No score given by this extender.\", \"error\", err, \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"extender\", extenders[extIndex].Name())\n810: \t\t\t\t\treturn\n811: \t\t\t\t}\n812: \t\t\t\tmu.Lock()\n813: \t\t\t\tdefer mu.Unlock()\n814: \t\t\t\tfor i := range *prioritizedList {\n815: \t\t\t\t\tnodename := (*prioritizedList)[i].Host\n816: \t\t\t\t\tscore := (*prioritizedList)[i].Score\n817: \t\t\t\t\tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n818: \t\t\t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Extender scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"extender\", extenders[extIndex].Name(), \"node\", nodename, \"score\", score)\n819: \t\t\t\t\t}\n820: \n821: \t\t\t\t\t// MaxExtenderPriority may diverge from the max priority used in the scheduler and defined by MaxNodeScore,\n822: \t\t\t\t\t// therefore we need to scale the score returned by extenders to the score range used by the scheduler.\n823: \t\t\t\t\tfinalscore := score * weight * (framework.MaxNodeScore / extenderv1.MaxExtenderPriority)\n824: \n825: \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \\tcntOfMaxScore := 1\\n871: \\tselectedIndex := 0\\n872: \\t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\\n873: \\tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\\n879: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\\n880: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n881: \\t\\t}\\n882: \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; PreFilter could optionally\\n401: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n402: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n403: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n404: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n405: \\t//\\n406: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n407: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n408: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n409: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n410: \\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\\n411: \\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\\n412: \\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\\n413: \\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\\n414: \\t// Filter again on a specific node.\\n415: \\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\\n416: }\\n417: \\n418: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\\n419: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\\n420: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\\n421: // These plugins should return \\\"Success\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\" in Status.code.\\n422: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\\n423: // Anything other than \\\"Success\\\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\\n424: // running the pod.\\n425: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n426: \\tPlugin\\n427: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n428: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n429: \\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n444: \\tPlugin\\n445: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n446: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n447: \\t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\\n448: \\t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\\n449: \\t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n450: \\t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n451: \\t//\\n452: \\t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\\n453: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n454: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n455: \\t//\\n456: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n457: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n458: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n459: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n460: \\t//\\n461: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n462: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\\n463: \\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\\n464: \\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\\n465: \\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\\n466: }\\n467: \\n468: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \\\"PreScore\\\" plugin. A plugin may use this data to update internal\\n471: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\\n472: type PreScorePlugin interface {\\n473: \\tPlugin\\n474: \\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\\n475: \\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\\n476: \\t// the pod will be rejected\\n477: \\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\\n478: \\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n479: \\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\\n480: }\\n481: \\n482: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\\n483: type ScoreExtensions interface {\\n484: \\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \\\"Score\\\"\\n485: \\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\\n486: \\t// a success status.\\n487: \\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\\n488: }\\n489: \\n490: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Score\\\" plugins to rank\\n491: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\\n492: type ScorePlugin interface {\\n493: \\tPlugin\\n494: \\t// Score is called on each filtered node. All scoring plugins must return success or\\n496: \\t// the pod will be rejected.\\n497: \\tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\\n498: \\n499: \\t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\\n500: \\tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\\n501: }\\n502: \\n503: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\\n504: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\\n505: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\\n506: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\\n507: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\\n508: // rejection of the pod.\\n509: type ReservePlugin interface {\\n510: \\tPlugin\\n511: \\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\\n512: \\t// updated. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\\n518: \\t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\\n519: \\t// method for the same plugin was not called.\\n520: \\tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n521: }\\n522: \\n523: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreBind\\\" plugins.\\n524: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\\n525: type PreBindPlugin interface {\\n526: \\tPlugin\\n527: \\t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. These plugins are\\n537: \\t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\\n538: \\t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\\n539: \\t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\\n540: \\tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n541: }\\n542: \\n543: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Permit\\\" plugins.\\n544: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\\n545: type PermitPlugin interface {\\n546: \\tPlugin\\n547: \\t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\\n548: \\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\\n549: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n550: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n551: \\t// waiting. If any\n1030: // of these plugins returns any status other than Success/Skip, the given pod is rejected.\n1031: // When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n1032: // and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n1033: func (f *frameworkImpl) RunPreScorePlugins(\n1034: \tctx context.Context,\n1035: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n1036: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n1037: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n1038: ) (status *framework.Status) {\n1039: \tstartTime := time.Now()\n1040: \tskipPlugins := sets.New[string]()\n1041: \tdefer func() {\n1042: \t\tstate.SkipScorePlugins = skipPlugins\n1043: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.PreScore, status.Code().String(), f.profileName).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(startTime))\n1044: \t}()\n1045: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n1046: \tverboseLogs := logger.V(4).Enabled()\n1047: \tif verboseLogs {\n1048: \t\tlogger = klog.LoggerWithName(logger, \"PreScore\")\n1049: \t}\n1050: \tfor _, pl := range f.preScorePlugins {\n1051: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0@917ed05e89979783903c4ca4563f0fc4120df4e2/-/blob/pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go%3FL850-1050"}}}

Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler Files\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main Scheduler struct that orchestrates the scheduling loop, initializes frameworks, queues, and cache; implements the Run() method that starts the scheduling process\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Contains ScheduleOne() entry point and the two-phase scheduling pipeline (schedulingCycle and bindingCycle); implements findNodesThatFitPod, prioritizeNodes, selectHost\n\n### Framework Architecture\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreFilter, Filter, PostFilter, PreScore, Score, Reserve, Permit, PreBind, Bind, PostBind), Framework interface, CycleState, Status codes, and extension points\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — frameworkImpl implementation that instantiates and orchestrates plugins; implements all Run* methods (RunPreFilterPlugins, RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins, etc.)\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState passes mutable data between plugins within a scheduling cycle\n\n### Internal Components\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface defining pod/node state management with Assume/Forget/Add/Remove operations and snapshot semantics\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache implementation tracking assumed pods and node information with expiration policy\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot provides read-only view of cache state at beginning of scheduling cycle\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue manages pods to be scheduled with activeQ, backoffQ, and unschedulableQ; handles pod lifecycle\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Entry Point: Main Scheduling Loop\n1. **Scheduler.Run(ctx)** (scheduler.go:435)\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Run()` to start queue processor\n   - Spawns goroutine calling `sched.ScheduleOne()` in a loop\n\n### Phase 1: Per-Pod Scheduling (ScheduleOne)\n2. **Scheduler.ScheduleOne(ctx)** (schedule_one.go:66)\n   - Pops next pod from queue via `sched.NextPod()`\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulePod()` which routes to `sched.schedulePod()`\n   - If **schedulingCycle** succeeds, spawns async goroutine for **bindingCycle**\n\n3. **Scheduler.schedulePod()** (schedule_one.go:390)\n   - **Scheduling Cycle** orchestration:\n     - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod()` to filter nodes\n     - Calls `prioritizeNodes()` to score and rank nodes\n     - Returns ScheduleResult with suggested node\n\n### Scheduling Cycle: Finding Best Node\n4. **Scheduler.findNodesThatFitPod()** (schedule_one.go:442)\n   - Updates cache snapshot: `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n   - **Runs PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()`\n     - Returns PreFilterResult (may reduce candidate nodes to a subset)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** via `findNodesThatPassFilters()` (in parallel)\n     - Filters nodes based on framework and extender filters\n   - Returns list of feasible nodes\n\n5. **Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:679)\n   - Iterates through preFilterPlugins in order\n   - Each plugin can:\n     - Return Success with optional PreFilterResult (NodeNames subset)\n     - Return Skip (coupled Filter plugins are skipped)\n     - Return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable (stops immediately on latter)\n   - Merges PreFilterResults via intersection if multiple plugins filter nodes\n\n6. **Scheduler.findNodesThatPassFilters()** (schedule_one.go:573)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** in parallel via parallelize framework\n   - For each node: `fwk.RunFilterPlugins()` (all filter plugins run sequentially per node)\n   - Stops early if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached (based on percentageOfNodesToScore)\n\n7. **Framework.RunFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:842)\n   - Iterates through filterPlugins sequentially\n   - Each plugin returns Success or Unschedulable for a given node\n   - First failed plugin rejects the node; framework records plugin status\n\n### Scoring Phase: Ranking Feasible Nodes\n8. **prioritizeNodes()** (schedule_one.go:745)\n   - **Runs PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs Score plugins** via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs extenders** (parallel) if configured\n   - Combines all scores into NodePluginScores with TotalScore\n\n9. **Framework.RunScorePlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1089+)\n   - For each score plugin:\n     - Calls Score() for each feasible node (parallel across nodes)\n     - Calls NormalizeScore() to normalize all scores for that plugin (0-100)\n   - Aggregates scores from all plugins weighted by plugin weights\n\n10. **selectHost()** (schedule_one.go:863)\n    - Uses reservoir sampling from highest-scored nodes\n    - Returns top node and optionally top-N nodes for reporting\n\n### Assumption Phase: Optimistic Concurrency\n11. **Scheduler.schedulingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:138)\n    - After SchedulePod succeeds, calls `sched.assume()` to mark pod on chosen node\n    - **Runs Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()`\n    - **Runs Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()`\n    - If any plugin fails:\n      - Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` to cleanup\n      - Calls `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()` to undo assumption\n    - Returns on success or moves pod to next phase\n\n12. **Scheduler.assume()** (schedule_one.go:870+)\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.AssumePod()` to assume pod on node\n    - Cache updates nodeInfo with pod's resources\n\n13. **Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve()** (runtime/framework.go:1149)\n    - Iterates through reservePlugins\n    - Each plugin can reserve resources or perform setup for the pod\n    - Failure stops immediately and triggers Unreserve on all prior plugins\n\n14. **Framework.RunPermitPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1169)\n    - Each plugin returns Status and optional timeout\n    - Success: proceed immediately\n    - Wait: pod enters waiting pod map (framework tracks waiting state)\n    - Reject/Error: trigger cleanup (Unreserve + ForgetPod)\n\n### Phase 2: Binding Cycle (Async)\n15. **Scheduler.bindingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:264)\n    - **WaitOnPermit()**: If pod was permitted to wait, blocks here\n    - **RunPreBindPlugins()**: Pre-binding setup plugins\n    - **bind()**: Calls Bind plugins to actually bind pod\n    - **RunPostBindPlugins()**: Post-binding cleanup plugins\n\n16. **Framework.WaitOnPermit()** (runtime/framework.go:1186)\n    - Waits on permit.WaitingPods map for pod's UID\n    - Returns Success (approved) or Rejected (denied)\n\n17. **Scheduler.bind()** (schedule_one.go:958)\n    - **RunBindPlugins()**: Calls Bind plugins\n    - First plugin to return non-Skip binds pod (sets NodeName)\n    - Default Bind plugin writes binding to API server\n\n18. **Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1304)\n    - Informational only; no failure handling\n    - Plugins can perform cleanup after binding succeeds\n\n### Failure Handling\n19. **Scheduler.handleSchedulingFailure()** (schedule_one.go:1012)\n    - Called when schedulingCycle fails\n    - If PostFilterPlugins exist, runs preemption to evict lower-priority pods\n    - Calls failure handler which may requeue pod with backoff\n\n20. **Scheduler.handleBindingCycleError()** (schedule_one.go:324)\n    - Called when bindingCycle fails\n    - Cleans up: RunReservePluginsUnreserve() + ForgetPod()\n    - Moves related pods from unschedulable queue back to active/backoff queue\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Pattern: Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Concurrency\n\n**Problem Solved:**\n- Binding is slow (API server write) and can fail\n- Blocking scheduling on binding would be inefficient\n- Need to continue scheduling other pods while binding completes\n\n**Solution:**\n1. **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Find node and assume pod on it in cache\n2. **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Actually bind pod to cluster, with failure recovery\n\n**Key Insight:** Cache assumption creates optimistic lock\n- Pod is considered scheduled in cache immediately\n- Other pods can't use same resources (Assume adds pod to nodeInfo)\n- If binding fails, Forget removes pod and resources are returned to unschedulable queue\n- Other pods scheduled during binding period already see reserved resources\n\n### Plugin Framework: Extension Points\n\nThe framework defines **13 extension points** where plugins can hook in:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous):**\n- **PreFilter**: Early filtering (can skip Filter plugins entirely)\n- **Filter**: Feasibility check per node\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption/remediation if pod unschedulable\n- **PreScore**: Preparation before scoring (informational)\n- **Score**: Rank nodes 0-100 (parallel per plugin, serial per node)\n- **Reserve**: Resource booking after node chosen\n\n**Permit/Waiting:**\n- **Permit**: Gate before binding (can wait for external events)\n\n**Binding Cycle (Async):**\n- **PreBind**: Pre-binding setup (can still reject)\n- **Bind**: Actually bind pod (default writes to API server)\n- **PostBind**: Cleanup after successful binding (no failures)\n\n**Queue Management:**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Pre-enqueue filtering\n- **QueueSort**: Pod priority ordering\n- **EnqueueExtensions**: Event-driven requeuing hints\n\n### Component Interactions\n\n**1. SchedulingQueue ↔ Scheduler**\n- Queue holds unscheduled pods in activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulableQ\n- Scheduler.NextPod() pops highest-priority pod\n- Queue.Done(uid) marks pod done after binding\n- Queue.Activate() moves pods between queues on cluster events\n\n**2. Cache ↔ Framework**\n- Cache maintains assumed pod state and node information\n- UpdateSnapshot() captures cache state at scheduling cycle start\n- Framework.SnapshotSharedLister() provides read-only view to plugins\n- AssumePod() is called after Reserve plugins pass\n- ForgetPod() reverts assumption on failure\n\n**3. CycleState ↔ Plugins**\n- CycleState is thread-safe mutable map passed to each plugin\n- PreFilter plugins write initial computed state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and optionally update state\n- Reserve/Permit plugins register cleanup actions\n- PreFilterExtensions use state for incremental updates during preemption\n\n**4. Framework ↔ Extenders**\n- Legacy extensibility mechanism (pre-plugin era)\n- Extenders participate in Filter and Prioritize phases\n- Extenders run after framework plugins\n- Integration: DefaultPreemption plugin can coordinate with extenders\n\n### Data Flow: Pod Perspective\n\n```\nPod → SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n   ↓\nPod.Pop() → ScheduleOne()\n   ↓\nScheduling Cycle:\n   - PreFilter plugins: Extract pod requirements, filter nodes\n   - Filter plugins: Test pod feasibility on remaining nodes (parallel)\n   - PreScore plugins: Setup scoring state (informational)\n   - Score plugins: Rank feasible nodes (parallel per plugin)\n   ↓\n   Find best node via selectHost() → Assume pod on node in cache\n   ↓\n   Reserve plugins: Book resources\n   Permit plugins: Gate binding\n   ↓ (if all pass)\n   Binding Cycle (async goroutine):\n   - WaitOnPermit(): Wait for permit plugin approval\n   - PreBind plugins: Final checks\n   - Bind plugins: Write binding to API server\n   - PostBind plugins: Cleanup\n   ↓\nPod is scheduled (NodeName set, binding recorded)\n```\n\n### Parallelization Strategy\n\n**Parallel Operations:**\n- **Filter plugins**: Parallelized across nodes (via parallelize.Parallelizer)\n  - Each node tests all filter plugins sequentially\n  - Early termination stops other nodes if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached\n- **Score plugins**: Parallelized across nodes\n  - Each score plugin evaluates all nodes in parallel\n  - NormalizeScore is sequential per plugin\n- **Extenders**: Parallelized across extenders (via goroutines)\n  - Each extender runs independently with mutex for aggregating scores\n\n**Sequential Operations:**\n- Filter plugins per node (can't parallelize within single node)\n- PreFilter and PostFilter plugins (must run sequentially, early termination possible)\n- Reserve, Permit, PreBind plugins (state dependencies)\n\n### Error Handling Strategy\n\n**Success Paths:**\n- All PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit plugins return Success → pod assigned\n\n**Failure Paths:**\n\n1. **PreFilter or Filter Failure:**\n   - Triggers PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n   - PostFilter plugins can attempt to make pod schedulable\n   - If PostFilter returns Success + NominatingInfo, pod saved for retry\n   - If PostFilter returns Unschedulable, pod goes to unschedulableQ + backoff\n\n2. **Reserve Failure:**\n   - Immediately triggers Unreserve on all prior Reserve plugins\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod requeued to backoffQ\n\n3. **Permit Failure:**\n   - Same cleanup as Reserve failure\n   - If rejected, pod marked and won't be re-tried immediately\n\n4. **Binding Cycle Failure:**\n   - Reserve plugins Unreserved\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod moved to unschedulableQ or backoffQ based on failure reason\n   - Cluster events may trigger requeuing\n\n### Status Codes and Their Meanings\n\n- **Success**: Plugin succeeded, pod can continue or is OK\n- **Error**: Unexpected internal error; pod requeued to activeQ/backoffQ\n- **Unschedulable**: Pod can't fit but may fit after cluster changes (e.g., node capacity increases); pod backed off\n- **UnschedulableAndUnresolvable**: Pod fundamentally unschedulable; pod backed off but PostFilter won't help\n- **Wait** (Permit only): Pod waiting for external event; entered waiting pod map\n- **Skip**: PreFilter/PreScore can skip coupled Filter/Score plugins; BindPlugin can skip binding\n- **Pending** (Reserve/PreBind only): Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external component (e.g., DRA device driver)\n\n### Snapshot Design: Read-Consistency Guarantee\n\n**Why Snapshots?**\n- Plugins run over many milliseconds; cluster state changes during scheduling\n- Without snapshot, plugins could see inconsistent state\n- Snapshot provides frozen view at cycle start\n\n**When Taken:**\n- At start of schedulePod(): `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(nodeInfoSnapshot)`\n- Snapshot remains unchanged through PreFilter → Filter → PreScore → Score\n\n**Snapshot Guarantees:**\n- All Filter decisions based on same node state\n- Score plugins see same node state\n- If pod preempted nodes before score phase, preemption not reflected in snapshot\n\n**Binding Phase:**\n- Can't use snapshot (cluster state has changed during scoring)\n- Plugins use live informers instead\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase architecture combining **synchronous scheduling (find + assume) with asynchronous binding**. This decouples slow API operations from scheduling throughput.\n\nThe **plugin framework** provides 13 extension points with clear separation of concerns: filtering (feasibility), scoring (preference), reservation (resource booking), and binding (commitment). Plugins are orchestrated via a state machine with careful failure handling and recovery mechanisms.\n\n**Key architectural decisions:**\n1. **Optimistic concurrency**: Assume in cache, recover on binding failure\n2. **Snapshot consistency**: Frozen cache view for scheduling decisions\n3. **Progressive filtering**: Early termination when enough feasible nodes found\n4. **Parallel scoring**: Independent plugin evaluation across nodes\n5. **Permit gating**: External control over binding start (DRA, etc.)\n6. **Error recovery**: Unreserve cleanup on any phase failure\n\nThis design achieves high scheduling throughput while maintaining correctness and allowing extensibility via plugins.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2116,"cache_read_input_tokens":90832,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2116},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3ccaa45a-9b5b-4241-8382-be0fc917da6b","uuid":"36e1f23e-b438-46bd-ad64-004a03859a63"}

**pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface defining pod/node state management with Assume/Forget/Add/Remove operations and snapshot semantics\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache implementation tracking assumed pods and node information with expiration policy\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot provides read-only view of cache state at beginning of scheduling cycle\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue manages pods to be scheduled with activeQ, backoffQ, and unschedulableQ; handles pod lifecycle\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### Entry Point: Main Scheduling Loop\n1. **Scheduler.Run(ctx)** (scheduler.go:435)\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Run()` to start queue processor\n   - Spawns goroutine calling `sched.ScheduleOne()` in a loop\n\n### Phase 1: Per-Pod Scheduling (ScheduleOne)\n2. **Scheduler.ScheduleOne(ctx)** (schedule_one.go:66)\n   - Pops next pod from queue via `sched.NextPod()`\n   - Calls `sched.SchedulePod()` which routes to `sched.schedulePod()`\n   - If **schedulingCycle** succeeds, spawns async goroutine for **bindingCycle**\n\n3. **Scheduler.schedulePod()** (schedule_one.go:390)\n   - **Scheduling Cycle** orchestration:\n     - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod()` to filter nodes\n     - Calls `prioritizeNodes()` to score and rank nodes\n     - Returns ScheduleResult with suggested node\n\n### Scheduling Cycle: Finding Best Node\n4. **Scheduler.findNodesThatFitPod()** (schedule_one.go:442)\n   - Updates cache snapshot: `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()`\n   - **Runs PreFilter plugins** via `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()`\n     - Returns PreFilterResult (may reduce candidate nodes to a subset)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** via `findNodesThatPassFilters()` (in parallel)\n     - Filters nodes based on framework and extender filters\n   - Returns list of feasible nodes\n\n5. **Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:679)\n   - Iterates through preFilterPlugins in order\n   - Each plugin can:\n     - Return Success with optional PreFilterResult (NodeNames subset)\n     - Return Skip (coupled Filter plugins are skipped)\n     - Return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable (stops immediately on latter)\n   - Merges PreFilterResults via intersection if multiple plugins filter nodes\n\n6. **Scheduler.findNodesThatPassFilters()** (schedule_one.go:573)\n   - **Runs Filter plugins** in parallel via parallelize framework\n   - For each node: `fwk.RunFilterPlugins()` (all filter plugins run sequentially per node)\n   - Stops early if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached (based on percentageOfNodesToScore)\n\n7. **Framework.RunFilterPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:842)\n   - Iterates through filterPlugins sequentially\n   - Each plugin returns Success or Unschedulable for a given node\n   - First failed plugin rejects the node; framework records plugin status\n\n### Scoring Phase: Ranking Feasible Nodes\n8. **prioritizeNodes()** (schedule_one.go:745)\n   - **Runs PreScore plugins** via `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs Score plugins** via `fwk.RunScorePlugins()`\n   - **Runs extenders** (parallel) if configured\n   - Combines all scores into NodePluginScores with TotalScore\n\n9. **Framework.RunScorePlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1089+)\n   - For each score plugin:\n     - Calls Score() for each feasible node (parallel across nodes)\n     - Calls NormalizeScore() to normalize all scores for that plugin (0-100)\n   - Aggregates scores from all plugins weighted by plugin weights\n\n10. **selectHost()** (schedule_one.go:863)\n    - Uses reservoir sampling from highest-scored nodes\n    - Returns top node and optionally top-N nodes for reporting\n\n### Assumption Phase: Optimistic Concurrency\n11. **Scheduler.schedulingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:138)\n    - After SchedulePod succeeds, calls `sched.assume()` to mark pod on chosen node\n    - **Runs Reserve plugins** via `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()`\n    - **Runs Permit plugins** via `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()`\n    - If any plugin fails:\n      - Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` to cleanup\n      - Calls `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()` to undo assumption\n    - Returns on success or moves pod to next phase\n\n12. **Scheduler.assume()** (schedule_one.go:870+)\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.AssumePod()` to assume pod on node\n    - Cache updates nodeInfo with pod's resources\n\n13. **Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve()** (runtime/framework.go:1149)\n    - Iterates through reservePlugins\n    - Each plugin can reserve resources or perform setup for the pod\n    - Failure stops immediately and triggers Unreserve on all prior plugins\n\n14. **Framework.RunPermitPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1169)\n    - Each plugin returns Status and optional timeout\n    - Success: proceed immediately\n    - Wait: pod enters waiting pod map (framework tracks waiting state)\n    - Reject/Error: trigger cleanup (Unreserve + ForgetPod)\n\n### Phase 2: Binding Cycle (Async)\n15. **Scheduler.bindingCycle()** (schedule_one.go:264)\n    - **WaitOnPermit()**: If pod was permitted to wait, blocks here\n    - **RunPreBindPlugins()**: Pre-binding setup plugins\n    - **bind()**: Calls Bind plugins to actually bind pod\n    - **RunPostBindPlugins()**: Post-binding cleanup plugins\n\n16. **Framework.WaitOnPermit()** (runtime/framework.go:1186)\n    - Waits on permit.WaitingPods map for pod's UID\n    - Returns Success (approved) or Rejected (denied)\n\n17. **Scheduler.bind()** (schedule_one.go:958)\n    - **RunBindPlugins()**: Calls Bind plugins\n    - First plugin to return non-Skip binds pod (sets NodeName)\n    - Default Bind plugin writes binding to API server\n\n18. **Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()** (runtime/framework.go:1304)\n    - Informational only; no failure handling\n    - Plugins can perform cleanup after binding succeeds\n\n### Failure Handling\n19. **Scheduler.handleSchedulingFailure()** (schedule_one.go:1012)\n    - Called when schedulingCycle fails\n    - If PostFilterPlugins exist, runs preemption to evict lower-priority pods\n    - Calls failure handler which may requeue pod with backoff\n\n20. **Scheduler.handleBindingCycleError()** (schedule_one.go:324)\n    - Called when bindingCycle fails\n    - Cleans up: RunReservePluginsUnreserve() + ForgetPod()\n    - Moves related pods from unschedulable queue back to active/backoff queue\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Pattern: Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Concurrency\n\n**Problem Solved:**\n- Binding is slow (API server write) and can fail\n- Blocking scheduling on binding would be inefficient\n- Need to continue scheduling other pods while binding completes\n\n**Solution:**\n1. **Scheduling Cycle** (synchronous): Find node and assume pod on it in cache\n2. **Binding Cycle** (asynchronous): Actually bind pod to cluster, with failure recovery\n\n**Key Insight:** Cache assumption creates optimistic lock\n- Pod is considered scheduled in cache immediately\n- Other pods can't use same resources (Assume adds pod to nodeInfo)\n- If binding fails, Forget removes pod and resources are returned to unschedulable queue\n- Other pods scheduled during binding period already see reserved resources\n\n### Plugin Framework: Extension Points\n\nThe framework defines **13 extension points** where plugins can hook in:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous):**\n- **PreFilter**: Early filtering (can skip Filter plugins entirely)\n- **Filter**: Feasibility check per node\n- **PostFilter**: Preemption/remediation if pod unschedulable\n- **PreScore**: Preparation before scoring (informational)\n- **Score**: Rank nodes 0-100 (parallel per plugin, serial per node)\n- **Reserve**: Resource booking after node chosen\n\n**Permit/Waiting:**\n- **Permit**: Gate before binding (can wait for external events)\n\n**Binding Cycle (Async):**\n- **PreBind**: Pre-binding setup (can still reject)\n- **Bind**: Actually bind pod (default writes to API server)\n- **PostBind**: Cleanup after successful binding (no failures)\n\n**Queue Management:**\n- **PreEnqueue**: Pre-enqueue filtering\n- **QueueSort**: Pod priority ordering\n- **EnqueueExtensions**: Event-driven requeuing hints\n\n### Component Interactions\n\n**1. SchedulingQueue ↔ Scheduler**\n- Queue holds unscheduled pods in activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulableQ\n- Scheduler.NextPod() pops highest-priority pod\n- Queue.Done(uid) marks pod done after binding\n- Queue.Activate() moves pods between queues on cluster events\n\n**2. Cache ↔ Framework**\n- Cache maintains assumed pod state and node information\n- UpdateSnapshot() captures cache state at scheduling cycle start\n- Framework.SnapshotSharedLister() provides read-only view to plugins\n- AssumePod() is called after Reserve plugins pass\n- ForgetPod() reverts assumption on failure\n\n**3. CycleState ↔ Plugins**\n- CycleState is thread-safe mutable map passed to each plugin\n- PreFilter plugins write initial computed state\n- Filter/Score plugins read and optionally update state\n- Reserve/Permit plugins register cleanup actions\n- PreFilterExtensions use state for incremental updates during preemption\n\n**4. Framework ↔ Extenders**\n- Legacy extensibility mechanism (pre-plugin era)\n- Extenders participate in Filter and Prioritize phases\n- Extenders run after framework plugins\n- Integration: DefaultPreemption plugin can coordinate with extenders\n\n### Data Flow: Pod Perspective\n\n```\nPod → SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n   ↓\nPod.Pop() → ScheduleOne()\n   ↓\nScheduling Cycle:\n   - PreFilter plugins: Extract pod requirements, filter nodes\n   - Filter plugins: Test pod feasibility on remaining nodes (parallel)\n   - PreScore plugins: Setup scoring state (informational)\n   - Score plugins: Rank feasible nodes (parallel per plugin)\n   ↓\n   Find best node via selectHost() → Assume pod on node in cache\n   ↓\n   Reserve plugins: Book resources\n   Permit plugins: Gate binding\n   ↓ (if all pass)\n   Binding Cycle (async goroutine):\n   - WaitOnPermit(): Wait for permit plugin approval\n   - PreBind plugins: Final checks\n   - Bind plugins: Write binding to API server\n   - PostBind plugins: Cleanup\n   ↓\nPod is scheduled (NodeName set, binding recorded)\n```\n\n### Parallelization Strategy\n\n**Parallel Operations:**\n- **Filter plugins**: Parallelized across nodes (via parallelize.Parallelizer)\n  - Each node tests all filter plugins sequentially\n  - Early termination stops other nodes if numFeasibleNodesToFind reached\n- **Score plugins**: Parallelized across nodes\n  - Each score plugin evaluates all nodes in parallel\n  - NormalizeScore is sequential per plugin\n- **Extenders**: Parallelized across extenders (via goroutines)\n  - Each extender runs independently with mutex for aggregating scores\n\n**Sequential Operations:**\n- Filter plugins per node (can't parallelize within single node)\n- PreFilter and PostFilter plugins (must run sequentially, early termination possible)\n- Reserve, Permit, PreBind plugins (state dependencies)\n\n### Error Handling Strategy\n\n**Success Paths:**\n- All PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit plugins return Success → pod assigned\n\n**Failure Paths:**\n\n1. **PreFilter or Filter Failure:**\n   - Triggers PostFilter plugins (preemption)\n   - PostFilter plugins can attempt to make pod schedulable\n   - If PostFilter returns Success + NominatingInfo, pod saved for retry\n   - If PostFilter returns Unschedulable, pod goes to unschedulableQ + backoff\n\n2. **Reserve Failure:**\n   - Immediately triggers Unreserve on all prior Reserve plugins\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod requeued to backoffQ\n\n3. **Permit Failure:**\n   - Same cleanup as Reserve failure\n   - If rejected, pod marked and won't be re-tried immediately\n\n4. **Binding Cycle Failure:**\n   - Reserve plugins Unreserved\n   - Cache.ForgetPod() removes assumption\n   - Pod moved to unschedulableQ or backoffQ based on failure reason\n   - Cluster events may trigger requeuing\n\n### Status Codes and Their Meanings\n\n- **Success**: Plugin succeeded, pod can continue or is OK\n- **Error**: Unexpected internal error; pod requeued to activeQ/backoffQ\n- **Unschedulable**: Pod can't fit but may fit after cluster changes (e.g., node capacity increases); pod backed off\n- **UnschedulableAndUnresolvable**: Pod fundamentally unschedulable; pod backed off but PostFilter won't help\n- **Wait** (Permit only): Pod waiting for external event; entered waiting pod map\n- **Skip**: PreFilter/PreScore can skip coupled Filter/Score plugins; BindPlugin can skip binding\n- **Pending** (Reserve/PreBind only): Scheduling succeeded but waiting for external component (e.g., DRA device driver)\n\n### Snapshot Design: Read-Consistency Guarantee\n\n**Why Snapshots?**\n- Plugins run over many milliseconds; cluster state changes during scheduling\n- Without snapshot, plugins could see inconsistent state\n- Snapshot provides frozen view at cycle start\n\n**When Taken:**\n- At start of schedulePod(): `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(nodeInfoSnapshot)`\n- Snapshot remains unchanged through PreFilter → Filter → PreScore → Score\n\n**Snapshot Guarantees:**\n- All Filter decisions based on same node state\n- Score plugins see same node state\n- If pod preempted nodes before score phase, preemption not reflected in snapshot\n\n**Binding Phase:**\n- Can't use snapshot (cluster state has changed during scoring)\n- Plugins use live informers instead\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase architecture combining **synchronous scheduling (find + assume) with asynchronous binding**. This decouples slow API operations from scheduling throughput.\n\nThe **plugin framework** provides 13 extension points with clear separation of concerns: filtering (feasibility), scoring (preference), reservation (resource booking), and binding (commitment). Plugins are orchestrated via a state machine with careful failure handling and recovery mechanisms.\n\n**Key architectural decisions:**\n1. **Optimistic concurrency**: Assume in cache, recover on binding failure\n2. **Snapshot consistency**: Frozen cache view for scheduling decisions\n3. **Progressive filtering**: Early termination when enough feasible nodes found\n4. **Parallel scoring**: Independent plugin evaluation across nodes\n5. **Permit gating**: External control over binding start (DRA, etc.)\n6. **Error recovery**: Unreserve cleanup on any phase failure\n\nThis design achieves high scheduling throughput while maintaining correctness and allowing extensibility via plugins.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
